# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# LLVM IR Type System to Code Generation Chain

## Your Task

Trace how LLVM IR types flow from the type creation API to code generation in llvm/llvm-project. Find C++ source files implementing: the Type class hierarchy (IntegerType, FunctionType, StructType), the type system's context ownership, and the IR type to machine type lowering in SelectionDAG.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d, sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d` (llvm/llvm-project)
- `sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333` (gcc-mirror/gcc)

62-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully traced the LLVM IR type system architecture and created a comprehensive answer file. Here's a summary of what I found:

## LLVM Type System Flow

**1. Type Class Hierarchy (Type Creation API)**
- `Type.h`: Base Type class with TypeID enumeration
- `DerivedTypes.h`: IntegerType, FunctionType, StructType class definitions  
- `Type.cpp`: Factory methods (IntegerType::get, FunctionType::get, StructType::get) with uniquing logic

**2. Context Ownership**
- `LLVMContext.h`: Public interface for context
- `LLVMContextImpl.h`: Private implementation containing type pools:
  - `IntegerTypes` (DenseMap): For arbitrary-width integers
  - `FunctionTypes` (FoldingSet): Uniqued function types using FunctionTypeKeyInfo
  - `AnonStructTypes` (DenseSet): Anonymous struct uniquing with AnonStructTypeKeyInfo
  - `NamedStructTypes` (StringMap): Named struct types
  - `ArrayTypes`, `VectorTypes`, `PointerTypes`: Other derived types
- BumpPtrAllocator for allocation without deallocation

**3. IR Type to Machine Type Lowering (SelectionDAG)**
- `SelectionDAG.h`: SelectionDAG declaration
- `TargetLowering.h`: Defines legal ValueTypes per target
- `LegalizeTypes.h`: DAGTypeLegalizer class (line 31)
- `LegalizeTypes.cpp`: Main entry point DAGTypeLegalizer::run() performing post-order DAG traversal
- Specialized legalization files handle different type classes:
  - LegalizeIntegerTypes.cpp: Integer promotion/expansion
  - LegalizeFloatTypes.cpp: Float softening/promotion
  - LegalizeVectorTypes.cpp: Vector scalarization/splitting
  - LegalizeTypesGeneric.cpp: Generic transformations

The answer file has been created at `/workspace/answer.json` with complete details about all key files, symbols, and the complete transformation chain from IR types through context uniquin

These are things like \\\"arrays of x\\\" or \\\"structure of x, y, z\\\" or\\n11: // \\\"function returning x taking (y,z) as parameters\\\", etc...\\n12: //\\n13: // The implementations of these classes live in the Type.cpp file.\\n14: //\\n15: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\\n16: \\n17: #ifndef LLVM_IR_DERIVEDTYPES_H\\n18: #define LLVM_IR_DERIVEDTYPES_H\\n19: \\n20: #include \\\"llvm/ADT/ArrayRef.h\\\"\\n21: #include \\\"llvm/ADT/STLExtras.h\\\"\\n22: #include \\\"llvm/ADT/StringRef.h\\\"\\n23: #include \\\"llvm/IR/Type.h\\\"\\n24: #include \\\"llvm/Support/Casting.h\\\"\\n25: #include \\\"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\\\"\\n26: #include \\\"llvm/Support/TypeSize.h\\\"\\n27: #include <cassert>\\n28: #include <cstdint>\\n29: \\n30: namespace llvm {\\n31: \\n32: class Value;\\n33: class APInt;\\n34: class LLVMContext;\\n35: template <typename T> class Expected;\\n36: class Error;\\n37: \\n38: /// Class to represent integer types. Secondly, a new\\n45:   // node may be passed to the legalization core, but when analyzed may morph\\n46:   // into a different node, leaving the original node as a NewNode in the DAG.\\n47:   // A node may morph if one of its operands changes during analysis. If a node morphs then the node it morphed into will\n54:   // be used instead of it for legalization, however the original node continues\n55:   // to live on in the DAG.\n56:   // The conclusion is that though there may be nodes marked NewNode in the DAG,\n57:   // all uses of such nodes are also marked NewNode: the result is a fungus of\n58:   // NewNodes growing on top of the useful nodes, and perhaps using them, but\n59:   // not used by them.\n60: \n61:   // If a value is mapped by ReplacedValues, then it must have no uses, except\n62:   // by nodes marked NewNode (see above).\n63: \n64:   // The final node obtained by mapping by ReplacedValues is not marked NewNode.\n65:   // Note that ReplacedValues should be applied iteratively.\n66: \n67:   // Note that the ReplacedValues map may also map deleted nodes (by iterating\n68:   // over the DAG we never dereference deleted nodes).  This means that it may\n69:   // also map nodes marked NewNode if the deallocated memory was reallocated as\n70:   // another node, and that new node was not seen by the LegalizeTypes machinery\n71:   // (for example because it was created but not used).  In general, we cannot\n72:   // distinguish between new nodes and deleted nodes.\n73:   SmallVector<SDNode*, 16> NewNodes;\n74:   for (SDNode &Node : DAG.allnodes()) {\n75:     // Remember nodes marked NewNode - they are subject to extra checking below.\n76:     if (Node.getNodeId() == NewNode)\n77:       NewNodes.push_back(&Node);\n78: \n79:     for (unsigned i = 0, e = Node.getNumValues(); i != e; ++i) {\n80:       SDValue Res(&Node, i);\n81:       bool Failed = false;\n82:       // Don't create a value in map.\n83:       auto ResId = ValueToIdMap.lookup(Res);\n84: \n85:       unsigned Mapped = 0;\n86:       if (ResId) {\n87:         auto I = ReplacedValues.find(ResId);\n88:         if (I != ReplacedValues.end()) {\n89:           Mapped |= 1;\n90:           // Check that remapped values are only used by nodes marked NewNode.\n91:           for (SDUse &U : Node.uses())\n92:             if (U.getResNo() == i)\n93:               assert(U.getUser()->getNodeId() == NewNode &&\n94:                      \"Remapped value has non-trivial use!\");\n95: \n96:           // Check that the final result of applying ReplacedValues is not\n97:           // marked NewNode.\n98:           auto NewValId = I->second;\n99:           I = ReplacedValues.find(NewValId);\n100:           while (I != ReplacedValues.end()) {\n101: ",

The private implementation LLVMContextImpl (llvm/lib/IR/LLVMContextImpl.h, lines 1759-1776) stores type pools:\\n\\n- DenseMap<unsigned, IntegerType*> IntegerTypes: Maps bit widths to IntegerType instances\\n- FoldingSet<FunctionType*> FunctionTypes: Hash set for function type uniquing using FunctionTypeKeyInfo (lines 1761-1762)\\n- DenseSet<StructType*> AnonStructTypes: Hash set for anonymous struct uniquing using AnonStructTypeKeyInfo (lines 1763-1764)\\n- StringMap<StructType*> NamedStructTypes: Named struct types\\n- DenseSet<TargetExtType*> TargetExtTypes: Target extension types using TargetExtTypeKeyInfo\\n- DenseMap<std::pair<Type*, uint64_t>, ArrayType*> ArrayTypes\\n- DenseMap<std::pair<Type*, ElementCount>, VectorType*> VectorTypes\\n- DenseMap<unsigned, PointerType*> PointerTypes\\n\\nEach Type also has a BumpPtrAllocator (Alloc member at line 1754) for allocation without deallocation.\\n\\n**IR Type to Machine Type Lowering in SelectionDAG:**\\n\\nThe type lowering pipeline begins when a SelectionDAG is created with IR types. The DAGTypeLegalizer class (llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/LegalizeTypes.h, line 31) orchestrates transformation from IR types to machine-legal ValueTypes (EVT).\\n\\nKey components:\\n\\n1. TargetLowering (llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/TargetLowering.h) defines which ValueTypes are legal and how operations should be transformed. The TLI field in DAGTypeLegalizer (line 32) provides getTypeAction() to determine how to handle each type: TypeLegal, Promote, Expand, SoftPromoteHalf, etc.\\n\\n2. DAGTypeLegalizer::run() (LegalizeTypes.cpp, lines 200-251) is the main entry point for type legalization. It walks the SelectionDAG in post-order, visiting leaf nodes first (ReadyToProcess state), then processing nodes as their operands are legalized.\\n\\n3. Type transformation maps track value transformations:\\n   - PromotedIntegers: Small integers promoted to larger types\\n   - ExpandedIntegers: Wide integers split into pairs\\n   - SoftenedFloats: Floating-point to integer conversion\\n   - PromotedFloats: Float precision promotion\\n   - ScalarizedVectors: Vectors reduced to scalars\\n   - SplitVectors: Wide vectors split\\n   - WidenedVectors: Small vectors widened\\n\\n4. Specialized legalization routines handle each type class:\\n   - LegalizeIntegerTypes.cpp: PromoteIntegerResult(), ExpandIntegerResult(), etc.\\n   - LegalizeFloatTypes.cpp: SoftenFloatResult(), PromoteFloatResult()\\n   - LegalizeVectorTypes.cpp: ScalarizeVectorResult(), SplitVectorResult()\\n   - LegalizeTypesGeneric.cpp: Generic expansion and promotion operations\\n\\nThe chain flows from IR Type\u2192LLVMContext uniquing\u2192SelectionDAG creation with IR types\u2192DAGTypeLegalizer analysis\u2192ValueType legalization\u2192machine-legal code generation.
